</tr><tr><td style="text-align:right;font-size:115%;padding-top: 0.6em;border-top:1px solid #006233;"><div class="plainlinks hlist navbar mini"><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Politics_of_the_Arab_League" title="Template:Politics of the Arab League"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Politics_of_the_Arab_League" title="Template talk:Politics of the Arab League"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Politics_of_the_Arab_League&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li></ul></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>The <b>Arab League</b> (<a href="/wiki/Arabic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a>: <span lang="ar" dir="rtl">الجامعة العربية</span>&#8206; <i><i lang="ar-Latn" title="Arabic-language romanization">al-Jāmiʻah al-ʻArabīyah</i></i>), formally the <b>League of Arab States</b> (<a href="/wiki/Arabic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a>: <span lang="ar" dir="rtl">جامعة الدول العربية</span>&#8206; <i><i lang="ar-Latn" title="Arabic-language romanization">Jāmiʿat ad-Duwal al-ʿArabīyah</i></i>), is a <a href="/wiki/Regional_organization" title="Regional organization">regional organization</a> of <a href="/wiki/Arab_world" title="Arab world">Arab states</a> in and around <a href="/wiki/North_Africa" title="North Africa">North Africa</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Horn_of_Africa" title="Horn of Africa">Horn of Africa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Arabia" class="mw-redirect" title="Arabia">Arabia</a>. It was formed in <a href="/wiki/Cairo" title="Cairo">Cairo</a> on 22 March 1945 with six members: <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Egypt" title="Kingdom of Egypt">Egypt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Iraq_(1932%E2%80%931958)" class="mw-redirect" title="Kingdom of Iraq (1932–1958)">Iraq</a>, <a href="/wiki/Emirate_of_Transjordan" title="Emirate of Transjordan">Transjordan</a> (renamed <a href="/wiki/Jordan" title="Jordan">Jordan</a> in 1949), <a href="/wiki/Lebanon" title="Lebanon">Lebanon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabia" title="Saudi Arabia">Saudi Arabia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">Syria</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Yemen" title="Yemen">Yemen</a> joined as a member on 5 May 1945. Currently, the League has <a href="/wiki/Member_states_of_the_Arab_League" title="Member states of the Arab League">22 members</a>, but <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">Syria</a>'s participation has been suspended since November 2011, as a consequence of government repression during the <a href="/wiki/Syrian_Civil_War" title="Syrian Civil War">Syrian Civil War</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The League's main goal is to "draw closer the relations between member States and co-ordinate collaboration between them, to safeguard their independence and sovereignty, and to consider in a general way the affairs and interests of the Arab countries".<sup id="cite_ref-yale_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-yale-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Through institutions, such as the <a href="/wiki/Arab_League_Educational,_Cultural_and_Scientific_Organization" title="Arab League Educational, Cultural and Scientific Organization">Arab League Educational, Cultural and Scientific Organization</a> (ALECSO) and the Economic and Social Council of the Arab League's <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Arab_Economic_Unity" title="Council of Arab Economic Unity">Council of Arab Economic Unity</a> (CAEU), the Arab League facilitates political, economic, cultural, scientific, and social programmes designed to promote the interests of the <a href="/wiki/Arab_world" title="Arab world">Arab world</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> It has served as a forum for the member states to coordinate their policy positions, to deliberate on matters of common concern, to settle some Arab disputes and to limit conflicts such as the <a href="/wiki/1958_Lebanon_crisis" title="1958 Lebanon crisis">1958 Lebanon crisis</a>. The League has served as a platform for the drafting and conclusion of many landmark documents promoting economic integration. One example is the <i><a href="/wiki/Joint_Arab_Economic_Action_Charter" title="Joint Arab Economic Action Charter">Joint Arab Economic Action Charter</a></i>, which outlines the principles for economic activities in the region.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:160px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Arab_League_of_states_establishment_-_Egypt_22-3-1945_22Millim_stamp.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/2/27/Arab_League_of_states_establishment_-_Egypt_22-3-1945_22Millim_stamp.jpg" decoding="async" width="158" height="260" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="158" data-file-height="260" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Arab_League_of_states_establishment_-_Egypt_22-3-1945_22Millim_stamp.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Arab League of states establishment memorial stamp. Showing flags of the 8 establishing countries: Kingdom of Egypt, Kingdom of Saudi Arabia, the Mutawakkilite Kingdom (North Yemen), Syrian Republic, Hashemite Kingdom of Iraq, Hashemite Kingdom of Jordan, Lebanese Republic</div></div></div>
<p>Each member state has one vote in the <i>League Council</i>, and decisions are binding only for those states that have voted for them. The aims of the league in 1945 were to strengthen and coordinate the political, cultural, economic and social programs of its members and to mediate disputes among them or between them and third parties. Furthermore, the signing of an agreement on <i>Joint Defence and Economic Cooperation</i> on 13 April 1950 committed the signatories to coordination of military defence measures. In March 2015, the Arab League General Secretary announced the establishment of a Joint Arab Force with the aim of counteracting extremism and other threats to the Arab States. The decision was reached while Operation Decisive Storm was intensifying in Yemen. Participation in the project is voluntary, and the army intervenes only at the request of one of the member states. The growing militarization of the region and the increase in violent civil wars as well as terrorist movements are the reason behind the creation of the JAF, financed by the rich Gulf countries.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In the early 1970s, the Economic Council of the League of Arab States put forward a proposal to create the Joint Arab Chambers of Commerce across the European states. That led, under the decree of the League of Arab States no. K1175/D52/G, to the decision by the Arab governments to set up the <a href="/wiki/Arab_British_Chamber_of_Commerce" title="Arab British Chamber of Commerce">Arab British Chamber of Commerce</a> which was mandated to "promote, encourage and facilitate bilateral trade" between the Arab world and its major trading partner, the United Kingdom.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Arab_League" title="History of the Arab League">History of the Arab League</a></div>
<p>Following adoption of the Alexandria Protocol in 1944, the Arab League was founded on 22 March 1945. It aimed to be a regional organisation of Arab states with a focus to developing the economy, resolving disputes and coordinating political aims.<sup id="cite_ref-History_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> Other countries later joined the league.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> Each country was given one vote in the council. The first major action was the joint intervention, allegedly on behalf of the majority Arab population being uprooted as the state of <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a> emerged in 1948 (and in response to popular protest in the Arab world), but a major participant in this intervention, Transjordan, had agreed with the Israelis to divide up the Arab Palestinian state proposed by the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> General Assembly, and Egypt intervened primarily to prevent its rival in <a href="/wiki/Amman" title="Amman">Amman</a> from accomplishing its objective.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>
It was followed by the creation of a mutual defence treaty two years later. A common market was established in 1965.<sup id="cite_ref-History_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_the_Arab_League" title="Geography of the Arab League">Geography of the Arab League</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Arab_League_members_colored_by_joining_date.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Arab_League_members_colored_by_joining_date.svg/220px-Arab_League_members_colored_by_joining_date.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="176" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Arab_League_members_colored_by_joining_date.svg/330px-Arab_League_members_colored_by_joining_date.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Arab_League_members_colored_by_joining_date.svg/440px-Arab_League_members_colored_by_joining_date.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1250" data-file-height="1000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Arab_League_members_colored_by_joining_date.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Joining dates of member states; the Comoros (circled) joined in 1993.<br /><span style="background-color:#f4eed7; color:black; border:1px solid darkgray; text-align:center;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;</span> 1940s <span style="background-color:#decd87; color:black; border:1px solid darkgray; text-align:center;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;</span> 1950s <span style="background-color:#c8ab37; color:black; border:1px solid darkgray; text-align:center;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;</span> 1960s <span style="background-color:#786721; color:white; border:1px solid darkgray; text-align:center;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;</span> 1970s</div></div></div>
<p>The Arab League member states cover over 13,000,000&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (5,000,000&#160;sq&#160;mi) and straddles two continents: <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">Africa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Asia" title="Asia">Asia</a>. The area largely consists of arid deserts, such as the <a href="/wiki/Sahara" title="Sahara">Sahara</a>. Nevertheless, it also contains several highly fertile lands like the <a href="/wiki/Nile_Valley" class="mw-redirect" title="Nile Valley">Nile Valley</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Jubba_Valley" title="Jubba Valley">Jubba Valley</a> and <a href="/wiki/Shebelle_Valley" title="Shebelle Valley">Shebelle Valley</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Horn_of_Africa" title="Horn of Africa">Horn of Africa</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Atlas_Mountains" title="Atlas Mountains">Atlas Mountains</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Maghreb" title="Maghreb">Maghreb</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Fertile_Crescent" title="Fertile Crescent">Fertile Crescent</a> that stretches over <a href="/wiki/Mesopotamia" title="Mesopotamia">Mesopotamia</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Levant" title="Levant">Levant</a>. The area comprises deep forests in southern <a href="/wiki/Arabian_Peninsula" title="Arabian Peninsula">Arabia</a> and parts of the world's longest river, the <a href="/wiki/Nile" title="Nile">Nile</a>.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Membership">Membership</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Member_states_of_the_Arab_League" title="Member states of the Arab League">Member states of the Arab League</a></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Charter_of_the_Arab_League" title="Charter of the Arab League">Charter of the Arab League</a>, also known as the Pact of the League of Arab States, is the founding treaty of the Arab League. Adopted in 1945, it stipulates that "the League of Arab States shall be composed of the independent Arab States that have signed this Pact."<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Initially, in 1945, there were only six members. Today, the Arab League has 22 members, including three African countries among the largest by area (<a href="/wiki/Sudan" title="Sudan">Sudan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Algeria" title="Algeria">Algeria</a> and <a href="/wiki/Libya" title="Libya">Libya</a>) and the largest country in the <a href="/wiki/Middle_East" title="Middle East">Middle East</a>, (<a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabia" title="Saudi Arabia">Saudi Arabia</a>). 
</p><p>Five countries have <a href="/wiki/Observer_status" title="Observer status">observer status</a>  that entitles them to express their opinion and give advice but denies them voting rights.<sup id="cite_ref-INDIAno_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-INDIAno-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> 
</p><p>There was a continual <a href="/wiki/Members_of_the_Arab_League" class="mw-redirect" title="Members of the Arab League">increase in membership</a> during the second half of the 20th century. As of 2016<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Arab_League&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, there are 22 member states:
</p>
<div class="div-col columns column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 15em; -webkit-column-width: 15em; column-width: 15em;">

</div>
<p>and 5 observer states:
</p>
<div class="div-col columns column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 15em; -webkit-column-width: 15em; column-width: 15em;">
<ul><li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/05/Flag_of_Brazil.svg/22px-Flag_of_Brazil.svg.png" decoding="async" width="22" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/05/Flag_of_Brazil.svg/33px-Flag_of_Brazil.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/05/Flag_of_Brazil.svg/43px-Flag_of_Brazil.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="720" data-file-height="504" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a></li>

</div>
<p>Libya was suspended on 22 February 2011, following the start of the <a href="/wiki/2011_Libyan_Civil_War" class="mw-redirect" title="2011 Libyan Civil War">Libyan Civil War</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/National_Transitional_Council" title="National Transitional Council">National Transitional Council</a>, the partially recognised interim government of Libya, sent a representative to be seated at the Arab League meeting on 17 August to participate in a discussion as to whether to readmit Libya to the organisation.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">Syria</a> was suspended on 16 November 2011. On 6 March 2013, the Arab League gave the <a href="/wiki/Syrian_National_Coalition" class="mw-redirect" title="Syrian National Coalition">Syrian National Coalition</a> Syria's seat in the Arab League.<sup id="cite_ref-syriannationalcoalition_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-syriannationalcoalition-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> On 9 March 2014, secretary general <a href="/wiki/Nabil_al-Arabi" class="mw-redirect" title="Nabil al-Arabi">Nabil al-Arabi</a> said that Syria's seat would remain vacant until the opposition completes the formation of its institutions.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics_and_administration">Politics and administration</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Charter_of_the_Arab_League" title="Charter of the Arab League">Charter of the Arab League</a>, <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_the_Arab_League" title="Politics of the Arab League">Politics of the Arab League</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Arab_Parliament" title="Arab Parliament">Arab Parliament</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Arab_Leage_HQ_977.PNG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Arab_Leage_HQ_977.PNG/220px-Arab_Leage_HQ_977.PNG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Arab_Leage_HQ_977.PNG/330px-Arab_Leage_HQ_977.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Arab_Leage_HQ_977.PNG/440px-Arab_Leage_HQ_977.PNG 2x" data-file-width="1225" data-file-height="918" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Arab_Leage_HQ_977.PNG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Headquarters of the Arab League, <a href="/wiki/Cairo" title="Cairo">Cairo</a>.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Israel-Palestine_Diplomacy.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Israel-Palestine_Diplomacy.svg/220px-Israel-Palestine_Diplomacy.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="112" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Israel-Palestine_Diplomacy.svg/330px-Israel-Palestine_Diplomacy.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Israel-Palestine_Diplomacy.svg/440px-Israel-Palestine_Diplomacy.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="853" data-file-height="433" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Israel-Palestine_Diplomacy.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #cdcd9c; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Recognition of both <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a> and Palestinian State</div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #FF4500; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Recognition of <a href="/wiki/State_of_Palestine" title="State of Palestine">Palestinian State</a> only</div></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Provinces_-_Arab_League.PNG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Provinces_-_Arab_League.PNG/200px-Provinces_-_Arab_League.PNG" decoding="async" width="200" height="101" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Provinces_-_Arab_League.PNG/300px-Provinces_-_Arab_League.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Provinces_-_Arab_League.PNG/400px-Provinces_-_Arab_League.PNG 2x" data-file-width="1563" data-file-height="786" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Provinces_-_Arab_League.PNG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Administrative divisions in the Arab League.</div></div></div>
<p>The Arab League is a political organization which tries to help integrate its members economically, and solve conflicts involving member states without asking for foreign assistance. It possesses elements of a state representative parliament while foreign affairs are often conducted under UN supervision.
</p><p>The Charter of the Arab League<sup id="cite_ref-yale_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-yale-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> endorsed the principle of an <a href="/wiki/Pan-Arabism" title="Pan-Arabism">Arab homeland</a> while respecting the <a href="/wiki/Sovereignty" title="Sovereignty">sovereignty</a> of the individual member states. The internal regulations of the Council of the League<sup id="cite_ref-haynes_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-haynes-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> and the committees<sup id="cite_ref-haynes2_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-haynes2-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> were agreed in October 1951. Those of the Secretariat-General were agreed in May 1953.<sup id="cite_ref-haynes3_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-haynes3-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Since then, governance of the Arab League has been based on the duality of supra-national institutions and the sovereignty of the member states. Preservation of individual statehood derived its strengths from the natural preference of ruling elites to maintain their power and independence in decision making. Moreover, the fear of the richer that the poorer may share their wealth in the name of <a href="/wiki/Arab_nationalism" title="Arab nationalism">Arab nationalism</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Arab_Cold_War" title="Arab Cold War">feuds among Arab rulers</a>, and the influence of external powers that might oppose Arab unity can be seen as obstacles towards a deeper integration of the league.
</p><p>Mindful of their previous announcements in support of the <a href="/wiki/Arabs" title="Arabs">Arabs</a> of <a href="/wiki/State_of_Palestine" title="State of Palestine">Palestine</a> the framers of the Pact were determined to include them within the League from its inauguration.<sup id="cite_ref-geddes_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-geddes-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> This was done by means of an annex that declared:<sup id="cite_ref-yale_5-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-yale-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<table class="cquote pullquote" role="presentation" style="margin:auto; border-collapse: collapse; border: none; background-color: transparent; width: auto;">
<tbody><tr>
<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: top; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: &#39;Times New Roman&#39;, Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: left; padding: 10px 10px;">“
</td>
<td style="vertical-align: top; border: none; padding: 4px 10px;">Even though Palestine was not able to control her own destiny, it was on the basis of the recognition of her independence that the Covenant of the League of Nations determined a system of government for her. Her existence and her independence among the nations can, therefore, no more be questioned <i>de jure</i> than the independence of any of the other Arab States. [...] Therefore, the States signatory to the Pact of the Arab League consider that in view of Palestine's special circumstances, the Council of the League should designate an Arab delegate from Palestine to participate in its work until this country enjoys actual independence
</td>
<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: bottom; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: &#39;Times New Roman&#39;, Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: right; padding: 10px 10px;">”
</td></tr>

</tbody></table>
<p>At the Cairo Summit of 1964, the Arab League initiated the creation of an organisation representing the Palestinian people. The first <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_National_Council" title="Palestinian National Council">Palestinian National Council</a> convened in <a href="/wiki/East_Jerusalem" title="East Jerusalem">East Jerusalem</a> on 29 May 1964. The <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_Liberation_Organization" class="mw-redirect" title="Palestinian Liberation Organization">Palestinian Liberation Organization</a> was founded during this meeting on 2 June 1964. Palestine was shortly admitted in to the Arab League, represented by the PLO. Today, <a href="/wiki/State_of_Palestine" title="State of Palestine">State of Palestine</a> is a full member of the Arab League.
</p><p>At the <a href="/wiki/Beirut_Summit" class="mw-redirect" title="Beirut Summit">Beirut Summit</a> on 28 March 2002, the league adopted the <a href="/wiki/Arab_Peace_Initiative" title="Arab Peace Initiative">Arab Peace Initiative</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-al-bab_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-al-bab-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> a Saudi-inspired peace plan for the <a href="/wiki/Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_conflict" title="Arab–Israeli conflict">Arab–Israeli conflict</a>. The initiative offered full normalisation of the relations with <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a>. In exchange, Israel was required to withdraw from all <a href="/wiki/Israeli-occupied_territories" title="Israeli-occupied territories">occupied territories</a>, including the <a href="/wiki/Golan_Heights" title="Golan Heights">Golan Heights</a>, to recognise Palestinian independence in the <a href="/wiki/West_Bank" title="West Bank">West Bank</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gaza_Strip" title="Gaza Strip">Gaza Strip</a>, with East Jerusalem as its capital, as well as a "just solution" for the <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_refugees" title="Palestinian refugees">Palestinian refugees</a>. The Peace Initiative was again endorsed at 2007 in the Riyadh Summit. In July 2007, the Arab League sent a mission, consisting of the <a href="/wiki/Jordan" title="Jordan">Jordanian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egyptian</a> foreign ministers, to Israel to promote the initiative. Following <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">Venezuela</a>'s move to expel Israeli diplomats amid the <a href="/wiki/2008%E2%80%932009_Israel%E2%80%93Gaza_conflict" class="mw-redirect" title="2008–2009 Israel–Gaza conflict">2008–2009 Israel–Gaza conflict</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kuwait" title="Kuwait">Kuwaiti</a> member of parliament <a href="/wiki/Waleed_Al-Tabtabaie" title="Waleed Al-Tabtabaie">Waleed Al-Tabtabaie</a> proposed moving Arab League headquarters to <a href="/wiki/Caracas,_Venezuela" class="mw-redirect" title="Caracas, Venezuela">Caracas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">Venezuela</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> On 13 June 2010, Amr Mohammed Moussa, Secretary-General of the Arab League, visited the <a href="/wiki/Gaza_Strip" title="Gaza Strip">Gaza Strip</a>, the first visit by an official of the Arab League since Hamas' armed takeover in 2007.
</p><p>In 2015, the Arab League voiced support for <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabian-led_intervention_in_Yemen" title="Saudi Arabian-led intervention in Yemen">Saudi Arabian-led military intervention in Yemen</a> against the <a href="/wiki/Zaidiyyah" title="Zaidiyyah">Shia Houthis</a> and forces loyal to former President <a href="/wiki/Ali_Abdullah_Saleh" title="Ali Abdullah Saleh">Ali Abdullah Saleh</a>, who was deposed in the <a href="/wiki/Yemeni_Revolution" title="Yemeni Revolution">2011 uprising</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 15 April 2018, in response to the <a href="/wiki/Turkish_military_operation_in_Afrin" class="mw-redirect" title="Turkish military operation in Afrin">Turkish invasion of northern Syria</a> aimed at ousting U.S.-backed <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Protection_Units" title="People&#39;s Protection Units">Syrian Kurds</a> from the enclave of <a href="/wiki/Afrin,_Syria" title="Afrin, Syria">Afrin</a>, the Arab League passed a resolution calling on Turkish forces to withdraw from Afrin.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In September 2019, the Arab League condemned <a href="/wiki/Benjamin_Netanyahu" title="Benjamin Netanyahu">Benjamin Netanyahu</a>'s plans to <a href="/wiki/Annexation" title="Annexation">annex</a> the eastern portion of the occupied <a href="/wiki/West_Bank" title="West Bank">West Bank</a> known as the <a href="/wiki/Jordan_Valley" title="Jordan Valley">Jordan Valley</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Military_of_the_Arab_League" title="Military of the Arab League">Military of the Arab League</a></div>
<p>The Joint Defence Council of the Arab League is one of the <a href="/wiki/Institutions_of_the_Arab_League" title="Institutions of the Arab League">Institutions of the Arab League</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ABC-CLIO_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ABC-CLIO-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> It was established under the terms of the <a href="/wiki/Joint_Defence_and_Economic_Co-operation_Treaty" title="Joint Defence and Economic Co-operation Treaty">Joint Defence and Economic Co-operation Treaty</a> of 1950 to coordinate the <a href="/wiki/Collective_security" title="Collective security">joint defence</a> of the Arab League <a href="/wiki/Member_states_of_the_Arab_League" title="Member states of the Arab League">member states</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Arab League as an Organization has no military Force, like the UN or EU, but at the 2007 summit, the Leaders decided to reactivate their joint defense and establish a peacekeeping force to deploy in South Lebanon, Darfur, Iraq, and other hot spots.
</p><p>At a 2015 summit in Egypt, member nations agreed in principle to form a joint military force.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

</div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economic_resources">Economic resources</span></h2>
<table class="box-More_citations_needed_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Arab_League&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.<br /><small><span class="plainlinks"><i>Find sources:</i>&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?as_eq=wikipedia&amp;q=%22Arab+League%22">"Arab League"</a>&#160;–&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?tbm=nws&amp;q=%22Arab+League%22+-wikipedia">news</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?&amp;q=%22Arab+League%22+site:news.google.com/newspapers&amp;source=newspapers">newspapers</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?tbs=bks:1&amp;q=%22Arab+League%22+-wikipedia">books</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//scholar.google.com/scholar?q=%22Arab+League%22">scholar</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.jstor.org/action/doBasicSearch?Query=%22Arab+League%22&amp;acc=on&amp;wc=on">JSTOR</a></span></small></span>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">March 2016</span>)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_the_Arab_League" title="Economy of the Arab League">Economy of the Arab League</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(PPP)" title="List of countries by GDP (PPP)">List of countries by GDP (PPP)</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(PPP)_per_capita" title="List of countries by GDP (PPP) per capita">List of countries by GDP (PPP) per capita</a></div>
<p>The Arab League is rich in resources, such as enormous <a href="/wiki/Oil" title="Oil">oil</a> and <a href="/wiki/Natural_gas" title="Natural gas">natural gas</a> resources in certain member states. Another industry that is growing steadily in the Arab League is telecommunications. Within less than a decade, local companies such as <a href="/wiki/Orascom" class="mw-redirect" title="Orascom">Orascom</a> and <a href="/wiki/Etisalat" title="Etisalat">Etisalat</a> have managed to compete internationally.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>Economic achievements initiated by the League amongst member states have been less impressive than those achieved by smaller Arab organisations such as the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_Cooperation_Council" title="Gulf Cooperation Council">Gulf Cooperation Council</a> (GCC).<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> Among them is the <a href="/wiki/Arab_Gas_Pipeline" title="Arab Gas Pipeline">Arab Gas Pipeline</a>, that will transport Egyptian and Iraqi gas to Jordan, Syria, Lebanon, and Turkey. As of 2013, a significant difference in economic conditions exist between the developed oil states of <a href="/wiki/Algeria" title="Algeria">Algeria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Qatar" title="Qatar">Qatar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kuwait" title="Kuwait">Kuwait</a> and the <a href="/wiki/UAE" class="mw-redirect" title="UAE">UAE</a>, and developing countries like <a href="/wiki/Comoros" title="Comoros">Comoros</a>, <a href="/wiki/Djibouti" title="Djibouti">Djibouti</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mauritania" title="Mauritania">Mauritania</a>, <a href="/wiki/Somalia" title="Somalia">Somalia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sudan" title="Sudan">Sudan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Yemen" title="Yemen">Yemen</a>.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:OAPEC_Members.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/OAPEC_Members.png/220px-OAPEC_Members.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="126" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/OAPEC_Members.png/330px-OAPEC_Members.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/OAPEC_Members.png/440px-OAPEC_Members.png 2x" data-file-width="825" data-file-height="472" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:OAPEC_Members.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/OAPEC" class="mw-redirect" title="OAPEC">OAPEC</a> Members</div></div></div>
<p>The Arab League also includes great fertile lands in the southern part of <a href="/wiki/Sudan" title="Sudan">Sudan</a>. It is referred to as the food basket of the <a href="/wiki/Arab_World" class="mw-redirect" title="Arab World">Arab World</a>, the region's instability including the independence of <a href="/wiki/South_Sudan" title="South Sudan">South Sudan</a> has not affected its <a href="/wiki/Tourism" title="Tourism">tourism</a> industry, that is considered the fastest growing industry in the region, with <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a>, <a href="/wiki/UAE" class="mw-redirect" title="UAE">UAE</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lebanon" title="Lebanon">Lebanon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tunisia" title="Tunisia">Tunisia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Jordan" title="Jordan">Jordan</a> leading the way. Another industry that is growing steadily in the Arab League is telecommunications.
</p><p>Economical achievements within members have been low in the league's history, other smaller Arab Organizations have achieved more than the league has, such as the <a href="/wiki/Cooperation_Council_for_the_Arab_States_of_the_Gulf" class="mw-redirect" title="Cooperation Council for the Arab States of the Gulf">GCC</a>, but lately several major economic projects that are promising are to be completed, the <a href="/wiki/Arab_Gas_Pipeline" title="Arab Gas Pipeline">Arab Gas Pipeline</a> is to end by the year 2010, Connecting Egyptian and Iraqi Gas to Jordan, Syria and Lebanon, and then to Turkey thus Europe, a free trade Agreement (<a href="/wiki/Greater_Arab_Free_Trade_Area" class="mw-redirect" title="Greater Arab Free Trade Area">GAFTA</a>) is to be completed by 1 January 2008, making 95% of all Arab Products tax free of customs.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_the_Arab_League" title="Transport in the Arab League">Transport in the Arab League</a></div>
<p>The Arab League is divided into five parts when it comes to transport, with the <a href="/wiki/Arabian_Peninsula" title="Arabian Peninsula">Arabian Peninsula</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Near_East" title="Near East">Near East</a> being entirely connected by air, sea, roads and railways. Another part of the League is the <a href="/wiki/Nile_Valley" class="mw-redirect" title="Nile Valley">Nile Valley</a>, made up of <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sudan" title="Sudan">Sudan</a>. These two member states have started to improve the River Nile's navigation system to improve accessibility and thus foster trading. A new railway system is also set to connect the southern Egyptian city of <a href="/wiki/Abu_Simbel" title="Abu Simbel">Abu Simbel</a> with the northern Sudanese city of <a href="/wiki/Wadi_Halfa" title="Wadi Halfa">Wadi Halfa</a> and then to <a href="/wiki/Khartoum" title="Khartoum">Khartoum</a> and <a href="/wiki/Port_Sudan" title="Port Sudan">Port Sudan</a>. The third division of the League is the <a href="/wiki/Maghreb" title="Maghreb">Maghreb</a>, where a 3,000&#160;km stretch of railway runs from the southern cities of <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">Morocco</a> to <a href="/wiki/Tripoli" title="Tripoli">Tripoli</a> in Western <a href="/wiki/Libya" title="Libya">Libya</a>. The fourth division of the League is the <a href="/wiki/Horn_of_Africa" title="Horn of Africa">Horn of Africa</a>, whose member states include <a href="/wiki/Djibouti" title="Djibouti">Djibouti</a> and <a href="/wiki/Somalia" title="Somalia">Somalia</a>. These two Arab League states are separated by only ten nautical miles from the Arabian Peninsula by the <a href="/wiki/Bab_el_Mandeb" class="mw-redirect" title="Bab el Mandeb">Bab el Mandeb</a> and this is quickly changing as Tarik bin Laden, the brother of <a href="/wiki/Osama_bin_Laden" title="Osama bin Laden">Osama bin Laden</a>, has initiated the construction of the ambitious <a href="/wiki/Bridge_of_the_Horns" title="Bridge of the Horns">Bridge of the Horns</a> project, which ultimately aims to connect the <a href="/wiki/Horn_of_Africa" title="Horn of Africa">Horn of Africa</a> with the <a href="/wiki/Arabian_Peninsula" title="Arabian Peninsula">Arabian Peninsula</a> via a massive bridge. The project is intended to facilitate and accelerate the already centuries-old trade and commerce between the two regions. The last division of the League is the isolated island of <a href="/wiki/Comoros" title="Comoros">Comoros</a>, which is not physically connected to any other Arab state, but still trades with other League members.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Literacy_in_Arab_league_countries">Literacy in Arab league countries</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_literacy_rate" title="List of countries by literacy rate">List of countries by literacy rate</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Arab_literacy_rate_(2010).svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Arab_literacy_rate_%282010%29.svg/220px-Arab_literacy_rate_%282010%29.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="176" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Arab_literacy_rate_%282010%29.svg/330px-Arab_literacy_rate_%282010%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Arab_literacy_rate_%282010%29.svg/440px-Arab_literacy_rate_%282010%29.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Arab_literacy_rate_(2010).svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Literacy rate in Arab World.</div></div></div>
<p>In collecting literacy data, many countries estimate the number of literate people based on self-reported data. Some use educational attainment data as a proxy, but measures of school attendance or grade completion may differ. Because definitions and data collection methods vary across countries, literacy estimates should be used with caution. <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Development_Programme" title="United Nations Development Programme">United Nations Development Programme</a>, <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Report" title="Human Development Report">Human Development Report</a> 2010. It is also important to note that the <a href="/wiki/Persian_Gulf" title="Persian Gulf">Persian Gulf</a> region has had an <a href="/wiki/Oil_boom" title="Oil boom">oil boom</a>, enabling more schools and universities to be set up.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_the_Arab_League" title="Demographics of the Arab League">Demographics of the Arab League</a></div>
<p>The Arab League is a culturally and ethnically one association of 22 member states, with the overwhelming majority of the League's population identified as <a href="/wiki/Arab" class="mw-redirect" title="Arab">Arab</a> (on a cultural ethnoracial basis). As of July 1, 2013, about 359 million people live in the states of the Arab League. Its population grows faster than in most other global regions. The most populous member state is <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a>, with a population of about 91 million.<sup id="cite_ref-Central_Agency_for_Public_Mobilization_And_Statistics_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Central_Agency_for_Public_Mobilization_And_Statistics-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> The least populated is the <a href="/wiki/Comoros" title="Comoros">Comoros</a>, with over 0.6 million inhabitants.
</p>

<ul><li>Syrian demographics are before the Syrian civil war.</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span></h3>
<p>The majority of the Arab League's citizens adhere to <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a>, with <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a> being the second largest religion. At least 15 million Christians combined live in <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraq</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jordan" title="Jordan">Jordan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lebanon" title="Lebanon">Lebanon</a>, <a href="/wiki/State_of_Palestine" title="State of Palestine">Palestine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sudan" title="Sudan">Sudan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">Syria</a>. In addition, there are smaller but significant numbers of <a href="/wiki/Druze" title="Druze">Druze</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yazidis" title="Yazidis">Yazidis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shabak_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Shabak people">Shabaks</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mandaeans" title="Mandaeans">Mandaeans</a>. Numbers for nonreligious <a href="/wiki/Arabs" title="Arabs">Arabs</a> are generally not available, but research by the <a href="/wiki/Pew_Forum" class="mw-redirect" title="Pew Forum">Pew Forum</a> suggests around 1% of people in the <a href="/wiki/MENA" title="MENA">MENA</a> region are "unaffiliated".<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Linguistics">Linguistics</span></h3>
<p>The official language of the Arab League is <a href="/wiki/Modern_Standard_Arabic" title="Modern Standard Arabic">Literary Arabic</a>, based on <a href="/wiki/Classical_Arabic" title="Classical Arabic">Classical Arabic</a>. However, several Arab League member states have other co-official or national languages, such as <a href="/wiki/Somali_language" title="Somali language">Somali</a>, <a href="/wiki/Afar_language" title="Afar language">Afar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Comorian_language" title="Comorian language">Comorian</a>, <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>, <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a>, <a href="/wiki/Berber_languages" title="Berber languages">Berber</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kurdish_languages" title="Kurdish languages">Kurdish</a>. In most countries, there is a dominant non-<a href="/wiki/Codification_(linguistics)" title="Codification (linguistics)">codified</a> <a href="/wiki/Varieties_of_Arabic" title="Varieties of Arabic">spoken Arabic dialect</a>.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sport_policies_of_the_Arab_League" title="Sport policies of the Arab League">Sport policies of the Arab League</a></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Pan_Arab_Games" title="Pan Arab Games">Pan Arab Games</a> are considered the biggest Arab sporting event, which brings together athletes from all the Arab countries to participate in a variety of different sports.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Union_of_Arab_Football_Associations" title="Union of Arab Football Associations">Union of Arab Football Associations</a> organises the <a href="/wiki/Arab_Nations_Cup" title="Arab Nations Cup">Arab Nations Cup</a> (for national teams) and the <a href="/wiki/Arab_Club_Champions_Cup" title="Arab Club Champions Cup">Arab Club Champions Cup</a> (for clubs). Arab sport federations also exist for several games, include <a href="/wiki/Basketball" title="Basketball">basketball</a>, <a href="/wiki/Volleyball" title="Volleyball">volleyball</a>, <a href="/wiki/Team_handball" class="mw-redirect" title="Team handball">handball</a>, <a href="/wiki/Table_tennis" title="Table tennis">table tennis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tennis" title="Tennis">tennis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Squash_(sport)" title="Squash (sport)">squash</a> and <a href="/wiki/Swimming_(sport)" title="Swimming (sport)">swimming</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
